However, the Spanish national team sacked Lopetegui a day prior to the tournament, stating that he had negotiated terms with the club without informing them.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-154)[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-155) The club then began re-shaping the squad in the summer of 2018, which included the sale of Cristiano Ronaldo to Juventus for a reported €117 million.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-156) Madrid began their [2018–19 campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2018–19 Real Madrid CF season") by losing to Atlético Madrid 2–4 [a.e.t.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overtime_\(sports\)#Association_football "Overtime \(sports\)") in the [2018 UEFA Super Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_UEFA_Super_Cup "2018 UEFA Super Cup"). After a 1–5 loss to Barcelona in _El Clásico_ on 28 October which left Real Madrid in the ninth place with only 14 points after ten games, Lopetegui was dismissed a day later and replaced by then [Castilla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_Castilla "Real Madrid Castilla") coach, [Santiago Solari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Solari "Santiago Solari").[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-157) On 22 December 2018, Real Madrid beat [Al Ain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Ain_FC "Al Ain FC") 4–1 in the [FIFA Club World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_FIFA_Club_World_Cup "2018 FIFA Club World Cup") and became the outright record winners of the Club World Cup with four titles.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_becomes_highest_trophy_holder_in_FIFA_Club_World_Cup-158) However, they were then knocked out of the [Copa del Rey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Copa_del_Rey "2018–19 Copa del Rey") at the semi-final stage by Barcelona, losing 1–4 on aggregate. On 5 March 2019, Real was defeated by [Ajax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AFC_Ajax "AFC Ajax") 1–4 (3–5 on aggregate) at home, crashing out of the [Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Champions_League "2018–19 UEFA Champions League") at the round of 16 stage after eight consecutive semi-finals appearances. On 11 March 2019, Real Madrid dismissed Solari and reinstated Zidane as the head coach of the club.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-159) Madrid finished the season with 68 points and a +17 goal difference, its lowest totals since [2001–02](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_La_Liga "2001–02 La Liga") and [1999–2000](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_La_Liga "1999–2000 La Liga") respectively.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-160)
In the summer of 2019, Madrid signed [Eden Hazard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eden_Hazard "Eden Hazard"), [Luka Jović](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luka_Jovi%C4%87 "Luka Jović"), [Éder Militão](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89der_Milit%C3%A3o "Éder Militão"), [Ferland Mendy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferland_Mendy "Ferland Mendy"), [Rodrygo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rodrygo "Rodrygo"), [Reinier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinier_Jesus_Carvalho "Reinier Jesus Carvalho") and other players for a total of more than €350 million.[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-161) On 12 January 2020, Madrid beat cross-city rivals Atlético Madrid in a penalty shootout in the [Supercopa de España final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a_Final "2020 Supercopa de España Final") to win their eleventh title.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-162) After a three-month hiatus due to the [COVID-19 outbreak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Spain "COVID-19 pandemic in Spain") in March 2020, [La Liga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_La_Liga "2019–20 La Liga") was restarted in June and Madrid won ten games in a row to capture the team's 34th league title, collecting 87 points in total.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-163) From the competition's resumption in June and until the end of the [2020–21 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2020–21 Real Madrid CF season"), Real temporarily played home fixtures at the [Alfredo Di Stéfano Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano_Stadium "Alfredo Di Stéfano Stadium"), while the Santiago Bernabéu underwent extensive renovations.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-164)[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Evening_Standard-165)
#### Further domestic success and _La Decimocuarta_
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Ofrenda_de_la_Liga_y_la_Champions-57-L.Mill%C3%A1n_%2852109310843%29.jpg/250px-Ofrenda_de_la_Liga_y_la_Champions-57-L.Mill%C3%A1n_%2852109310843%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ofrenda_de_la_Liga_y_la_Champions-57-L.Mill%C3%A1n_\(52109310843\).jpg)Real Madrid players celebrating the [double](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_\(association_football\)#European_double "Double \(association football\)") on 29 May 2022, the day after their Champions League victory
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/250px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg)
[**Courtois**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thibaut_Courtois "Thibaut Courtois")
[**Militão**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89der_Milit%C3%A3o "Éder Militão")
[**Alaba**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Alaba "David Alaba")

[**Mendy**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferland_Mendy "Ferland Mendy")
**[Casemiro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casemiro "Casemiro")**
[**Modrić**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luka_Modri%C4%87 "Luka Modrić")
[**Kroos**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toni_Kroos "Toni Kroos")
[**Valverde**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federico_Valverde "Federico Valverde")
[**Vinícius Jr.**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vin%C3%ADcius_J%C3%BAnior "Vinícius Júnior")
[**Benzema (C)**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karim_Benzema "Karim Benzema")
[2022 UEFA Champions League final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_UEFA_Champions_League_final "2022 UEFA Champions League final") starting lineup
Zidane left a second time on 27 May 2021 after going trophyless [that season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2020–21 Real Madrid CF season"),[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-166) with Carlo Ancelotti returning to coach the team for the [2021–22 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2021–22 Real Madrid CF season").[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-167) On the domestic front, he delivered two trophies out of possible three, winning [La Liga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_La_Liga "2021–22 La Liga") and the [Supercopa de España](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a "2021–22 Supercopa de España").[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-168)[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-169)[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-170) As such, Ancelotti won all six available top trophies at Madrid.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-171) In the [Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_UEFA_Champions_League "2021–22 UEFA Champions League"), Madrid produced one of the most memorable runs of all time,[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-172) defeating pre-tournament favourites [Paris Saint-Germain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C. "Paris Saint-Germain F.C."),[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-173)[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-174) [defending champions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Champions_League "2020–21 UEFA Champions League") and favourites [Chelsea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelsea_F.C. "Chelsea F.C."),[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-175) [Premier League champions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Premier_League "2020–21 Premier League") and heavy favourites [Manchester City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C. "Manchester City F.C."),[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-176) all in dramatic fashion,[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-177) and setting up the [final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2022 UEFA Champions League Final") against Liverpool, who were once again widely considered as favourites,[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-178) in a rematch of their 2018 encounter. A lone [Vinícius Júnior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vin%C3%ADcius_J%C3%BAnior "Vinícius Júnior") goal sealed the 14th European Cup for _Los Blancos_ , their fifth in nine years, and Ancelotti's second in charge.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-179)[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-180) Real also claimed their fourth ever [European double](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_\(association_football\)#European_double "Double \(association football\)") (after [1956–57](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1956%E2%80%9357_Real_Madrid_CF_season "1956–57 Real Madrid CF season"), [1957–58](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957%E2%80%9358_Real_Madrid_CF_season "1957–58 Real Madrid CF season"), and [2016–17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2016–17 Real Madrid CF season")). Despite Real's status as the most decorated team in the history of the Champions League, they were not favoured to win that year's edition, and their improbable run was widely considered a surprise.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-181)
#### Even more success and _La Decimoquinta_
After a highly successful 2021–22 season, Real Madrid signed German defender [Antonio Rüdiger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonio_R%C3%BCdiger "Antonio Rüdiger") and French midfielder [Aurélien Tchouaméni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aur%C3%A9lien_Tchouam%C3%A9ni "Aurélien Tchouaméni"), while club legends Marcelo, Isco, Gareth Bale and Casemiro left the club. Real Madrid's [2022–23](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2022–23 Real Madrid CF season") season began with lifting the [UEFA Super Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup "UEFA Super Cup") and later the [FIFA Club World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup "FIFA Club World Cup"). The season ended with Real Madrid winning the [2022–23 Copa del Rey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_Copa_del_Rey "2022–23 Copa del Rey"), but losing the La Liga and Spanish Super Cup to [Barcelona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona "FC Barcelona") and the Champions League to Manchester City, being defeated 5–1 on aggregate.
In 2023, Real Madrid signed [Jude Bellingham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jude_Bellingham "Jude Bellingham"), who was given the number #5 jersey, previously used by Zinedine Zidane. Real also signed [Arda Güler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arda_G%C3%BCler "Arda Güler") and [Fran García](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran_Garc%C3%ADa_\(footballer,_born_1999\) "Fran García \(footballer, born 1999\)"). Meanwhile, Vinícius Júnior was given the number #7 jersey, previously used by Raúl and Cristiano Ronaldo; while Rodrygo was given the number #11 jersey, previously used by Gareth Bale. [Karim Benzema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karim_Benzema "Karim Benzema") left the club, while [Toni Kroos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toni_Kroos "Toni Kroos") would later announce that he would retire from football after this season.
The [2023–24 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023%E2%80%9324_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2023–24 Real Madrid CF season") would prove to be another highly successful season for Los Blancos. First, Real Madrid lifted the Spanish Super Cup against Barcelona 4–1, taking revenge of the previous year's 3–0 defeat. Then, Real Madrid lifted the La Liga with relative ease, reaching 95 points, the second-best winning campaign by Real Madrid in La Liga history after the 2011–12 100 points season. In the [2023–24 UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023%E2%80%9324_UEFA_Champions_League "2023–24 UEFA Champions League"), Real Madrid knocked out [RB Leipzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RB_Leipzig "RB Leipzig") in the Round of 16, then defending champions [Manchester City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_City "Manchester City") in penalties.
In the semifinals, Real Madrid faced [Bayern Munich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayern_Munich "Bayern Munich") again. The first match was a 2–2 draw, while the second match in the Bernabéu was marked by a double by [Joselu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joselu "Joselu") in the last few minutes of the game, with Bayern Munich suffering a historic comeback after leading 1–0. Real Madrid faced [Borussia Dortmund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund "Borussia Dortmund") in the final, and won 2–0, with [Dani Carvajal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dani_Carvajal "Dani Carvajal") being the man of the match and scoring with a header after a Toni Kroos corner, and Vinícius Júnior once again scoring in a UCL final. Real Madrid won their 15th Champions League without losing a single match during the campaign.
Following the conclusion of the 2023–24 season, Real Madrid announced that striker [Kylian Mbappé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kylian_Mbapp%C3%A9 "Kylian Mbappé") would be joining the club on a free transfer from [Paris Saint-Germain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain "Paris Saint-Germain") in July 2024, concluding one of the most highly anticipated transfer sagas in modern history.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-182) On 18 December 2024, Real Madrid clinched their second trophy of the season, uplifting the inaugural [2024 FIFA Intercontinental Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_FIFA_Intercontinental_Cup "2024 FIFA Intercontinental Cup") by beating [Pachuca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C.F._Pachuca "C.F. Pachuca") 3–0.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-183)
## Crests and colours
### Crests
  * [![1902](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Real_emblem.png/120px-Real_emblem.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Real_emblem.png "1902")
1902
  * [![1908](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Escudo_Real_Madrid_1908.png/120px-Escudo_Real_Madrid_1908.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Escudo_Real_Madrid_1908.png "1908")
1908
  * [![1920](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Real_emblem_5.png/120px-Real_emblem_5.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Real_emblem_5.png "1920")
1920
  * [![1931](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Escudo_Real_madrid_1931.png/120px-Escudo_Real_madrid_1931.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Escudo_Real_madrid_1931.png "1931")
1931
  * [![2001](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/Real_Madrid_CF.svg/120px-Real_Madrid_CF.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Real_Madrid_CF.svg "2001")
2001


The first crest had a simple design consisting of a decorative interlacing of the three initials of the club, "MCF" for Madrid Club de Fútbol, in dark blue on a white shirt. The first change in the crest occurred in 1908 when the letters adopted a more streamlined form and appeared inside a circle.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Escudo_Real_Madrid-184) The next change in the configuration of the crest did not occur until the presidency of [Pedro Parages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pedro_Parages "Pedro Parages") in 1920. At that time, [King Alfonso XIII](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfonso_XIII "Alfonso XIII") granted the club his royal patronage which came in the form of the title "Real Madrid," meaning "Royal."[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-185) Thus, Alfonso's crown was added to the crest and the club styled itself _Real Madrid Club de Fútbol_.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Escudo_Real_Madrid-184)
With the dissolution of the monarchy in 1931, all royal symbols (the crown on the crest and the title of Real) were eliminated. The crown was replaced by the dark mulberry band of the Region of Castile.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(IV\)-48) In 1941, two years after [Nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_faction_\(Spanish_Civil_War\) "Nationalist faction \(Spanish Civil War\)") victory in the Civil War, the [Francoist regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francoist_Spain "Francoist Spain") restored the crest's "Real Corona", or "Royal Crown", while the mulberry stripe of [Castile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castile_\(historical_region\) "Castile \(historical region\)") was retained as well.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-goal.com-186)[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(V\)-57) In addition, the whole crest was made full color, with gold being the most prominent, and the club went back to its honorific name _Real Madrid Club de Fútbol_.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Escudo_Real_Madrid-184) The most recent modification to the crest occurred in 2001 when the club wanted to better situate itself for the 21st century and further standardize its crest. One of the modifications made was changing the mulberry stripe to a more bluish shade.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Escudo_Real_Madrid-184)
### Colours
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/40px-Commons-logo.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Commons-logo.svg)
Wikimedia Commons has media related to [Real Madrid CF kits (1902–2000)](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF_kits_\(1902%E2%80%932000\) "commons:Real Madrid CF kits \(1902–2000\)").
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/40px-Commons-logo.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Commons-logo.svg)
Wikimedia Commons has media related to [Real Madrid CF kits (2000–present)](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF_kits_\(2000%E2%80%93present\) "commons:Real Madrid CF kits \(2000–present\)").
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Real_Madrid_%281964%29.jpg/250px-Real_Madrid_%281964%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Real_Madrid_\(1964\).jpg)Real Madrid in 1964. Nicknamed _Los Blancos_ (The Whites), the club has worn an all-white home kit except for one season in 1925.
Real Madrid has maintained the white shirt for its home kit throughout the history of the club. There was, however, one season in 1926 that the shirt and shorts were not both white. It was an initiative undertaken by [Juan Padrós](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juan_Padr%C3%B3s "Juan Padrós") in honour of an English team [Corinthian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corinthian_F.C. "Corinthian F.C."), which he had met on one of his trips, one of the most famous teams at the time known for its elegance and sportsmanship.[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-sapiens.cat-43) It was decided that Real Madrid would wear black shorts in an attempt to replicate the English team, which had also inspired Madrid's original white kit, but the initiative lasted just one year. After being eliminated from the [1926 Copa del Rey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1926_Copa_del_Rey "1926 Copa del Rey") by Barcelona with a 1–5 defeat in Madrid and a 2–0 defeat in Catalonia, President Parages decided to return to an all-white kit, claiming that the other kit brought bad luck.[[note 3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Origin-187) By the early 1940s, the manager changed the kit again by adding buttons to the shirt and the club's crest on the left breast, which has remained ever since. On 23 November 1947, in a game against [Atlético Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid "Atlético Madrid") at the Metropolitano Stadium, Real Madrid became the first Spanish team to wear numbered shirts.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(V\)-57) English club [Leeds United](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C. "Leeds United F.C.") permanently switched their blue shirt for a white one in the 1960s, to emulate the dominant Real Madrid of the era.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-188)
Real's traditional away colours are all blue or all purple. Since the advent of the replica kit market, the club has also released various other one colour designs, including red, green, orange and black. The club's kit is manufactured by [Adidas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adidas "Adidas"), whose contract extends from 1998.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-189)[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-190) Real Madrid's first shirt sponsor, [Zanussi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zanussi "Zanussi"), agreed for the 1982–83, 1983–84 and 1984–85 seasons. Following that, the club was sponsored by [Parmalat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parmalat "Parmalat") and Otaysa before a long-term deal was signed with [Teka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teka "Teka") in 1992.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Evolución_Del_Uniforme_del_Real_Madrid_\(1902–1989\)-191)[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Evolución_Del_Uniforme_del_Real_Madrid_\(1991–2008\)-192) In 2001, Real Madrid ended their contract with Teka and for one season and used the Realmadrid.com logo to promote the club's website. Then, in 2002, a deal was signed with [Siemens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siemens "Siemens") and in 2006, the [BenQ Siemens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BenQ_Siemens "BenQ Siemens") logo appeared on the club's shirt.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-193) Real Madrid's shirt sponsor from 2007 until 2013 was [bwin.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bwin.com "Bwin.com") following the economic problems of BenQ Siemens.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-194)[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-195) Fly Emirates became their shirt sponsor in 2013, and in 2017 the club renewed the sponsorship with the airliner, signing a deal until 2022 worth €70 million per year.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-196) In 2022, the agreement was again extended, until 2026.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-197) In 2015, Madrid signed a new ten-year contract with Adidas, believed to be worth a total of £850 million (€1 billion), with the club earning £59 million (€64 million) per season. The contract includes a clause sanctioning penalty or agreement termination anytime, if Real Madrid fails to qualify for the European competitions or is relegated from [La Liga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Liga "La Liga").[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-198)
