## Grounds
Further information: [Estadio Chamartín](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadio_Chamart%C3%ADn "Estadio Chamartín"), [Santiago Bernabéu Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium"), and [Alfredo Di Stéfano Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano_Stadium "Alfredo Di Stéfano Stadium")
Santiago Bernabéu[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Estadio_Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_39.jpg/250px-Estadio_Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_39.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Estadio_Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_39.jpg)
---
[Capacity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seating_capacity "Seating capacity")| 85,000[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Capacity-203)
Field size| 107 m × 72 m (351 ft × 236 ft)[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-204)
Construction
[Broke ground](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groundbreaking "Groundbreaking")| 27 October 1944
Opened| 14 December 1947
Architect| Manuel Muñoz Monasterio, Luis Alemany Soler, Antonio Lamela
After moving between several grounds, the team relocated to the [Campo de O'Donnell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campo_de_O%27Donnell "Campo de O'Donnell") in 1912, which remained its home stadium for 11 years.[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-History_—_Chapter_1_-_From_the_Estrada_Lot_to_the_nice,_little_O'Donnel_pitch-45) After this period, the club moved for one year to the [Campo de Ciudad Lineal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campo_de_Ciudad_Lineal "Campo de Ciudad Lineal"), a small ground with a capacity of 8,000 spectators. After that, Real Madrid started playing its home matches at the [Estadio Chamartín](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadio_Chamart%C3%ADn "Estadio Chamartín"), which was inaugurated on 17 May 1923 with a match against [Newcastle United](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C. "Newcastle United F.C.").[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-205) In this stadium, which hosted 22,500 spectators, Real Madrid celebrated its first Spanish league title.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(III\)-47) Following his election in 1943, president [Santiago Bernabéu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_\(footballer\) "Santiago Bernabéu \(footballer\)") decided that the Chamartín was not big enough for the ambitions of the club, and thus a [new stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium") was built and inaugurated on 14 December 1947.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(V\)-57)[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-History-206) Initially knows as _Nuevo Chamartín_ , the stadium was renamed in honour of Bernabéu in 1955 and continues to bear his name to this day.[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(VI\)-58) The first match at the Bernabéu was played between Madrid and the Portuguese club [Belenenses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C.F._Os_Belenenses "C.F. Os Belenenses"), with _Los Blancos_ winning 3–1 and Sabino Barinaga scoring the first goal.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(V\)-57)
The capacity has changed frequently, peaking at 120,000 after a 1953 expansion.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-60th_Anniversary-207) Since then, there have been a number of reductions due to modernizations (the last standing areas were removed in 1998–99 in response to UEFA regulations which had forbidden standing at matches in European competitions), countered to some extent by expansions.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-60th_Anniversary-207) The current capacity is 81,044 spectators. Real Madrid has the fourth-highest average attendance in Europe, behind Borussia Dortmund, Barcelona and Manchester United.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-208)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-209)[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-210)[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-211)
The Bernabéu has hosted the [1964 UEFA European Championship final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_European_Nations%27_Cup_Final "1964 European Nations' Cup Final"), the [1982 FIFA World Cup final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup_Final "1982 FIFA World Cup Final"), and the [1957](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957_European_Cup_Final "1957 European Cup Final"), [1969](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969_European_Cup_Final "1969 European Cup Final"), [1980](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_European_Cup_Final "1980 European Cup Final") and [2010](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2010 UEFA Champions League Final") European Cup/Champions League finals.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-212) The stadium has its own namesake [Madrid Metro station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_\(Madrid_Metro\) "Santiago Bernabéu \(Madrid Metro\)") along the 10 line.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-213) On 14 November 2007, the Bernabéu was upgraded to [Elite Football Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_stadium_categories "UEFA stadium categories") status by UEFA.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-214)
On 9 May 2006, the [Alfredo Di Stéfano Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano_Stadium "Alfredo Di Stéfano Stadium"), named after club legend Alfredo Di Stéfano, was inaugurated in the Real Madrid City, where Real Madrid usually trains. The inaugural match was played between Real Madrid and [Reims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stade_de_Reims "Stade de Reims"), a rematch of the [1956 European Cup final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1956_European_Cup_Final "1956 European Cup Final"). Real Madrid 6–1, with goals from [Sergio Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Ramos "Sergio Ramos"), [Antonio Cassano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonio_Cassano "Antonio Cassano") (2), [Roberto Soldado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roberto_Soldado "Roberto Soldado") (2) and [José Manuel Jurado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Jurado "José Manuel Jurado"). The venue is now part of the [Ciudad Real Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciudad_Real_Madrid "Ciudad Real Madrid"), the club's training facility located outside Madrid, in Valdebebas. The stadium's capacity is 5,000 people, and it is [Real Madrid Castilla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_Castilla "Real Madrid Castilla")'s home ground.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-215) For the latter part of the [2019–20 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2019–20 Real Madrid CF season") and throughout the [2020–21 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2020–21 Real Madrid CF season"), the stadium hosted the first team's home games due to a combination of the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Spain "COVID-19 pandemic in Spain")-triggered restrictions and an extensive renovation of the Santiago Bernabéu.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-216)[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Evening_Standard-165)
The latest renovation of the Santiago Bernabéu is set to increase the capacity by approximately 4,000 with the addition of an extra tier, bringing it to nearly 85,000.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-217)[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-218) Furthermore, the height will also be increased by ten metres and a retractable roof, a retractable pitch and a 360-degree screen will be installed.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-219)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-220) The works have started in 2019, and the renovated stadium was initially planned to be unveiled in 2022; however, the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic") and [Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine") caused significant disruption to supply chains, prompting the club to postpone the stadium's inauguration to 2023.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-221)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-222)
## Records and statistics
Main article: [List of Real Madrid CF records and statistics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Real_Madrid_CF_records_and_statistics "List of Real Madrid CF records and statistics")
See also: [Real Madrid CF in international football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF_in_international_football "Real Madrid CF in international football")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Raul_Gonzalez_10mar2007.jpg/250px-Raul_Gonzalez_10mar2007.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Raul_Gonzalez_10mar2007.jpg)[Raúl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_\(footballer\) "Raúl \(footballer\)") is Real Madrid's all-time leader in appearances.
[Raúl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_\(footballer\) "Raúl \(footballer\)") holds the record for most appearances with Real Madrid, with 741 appearances from 1994 to 2010. [Iker Casillas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iker_Casillas "Iker Casillas") comes second with 725 appearances, followed by [Manuel Sanchis Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Sanchis_Hontiyuelo "Manuel Sanchis Hontiyuelo"), having played 710 times.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-223) The record for a goalkeeper is held by Iker Casillas, with 725 appearances. With 63 goals, [Cristiano Ronaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo "Cristiano Ronaldo") has scored the most international goals while playing for the club. Meanwhile, [Sergio Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Ramos "Sergio Ramos") has accumulated the most caps while playing for the club, with 176.
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Cristiano_Ajax.jpg/250px-Cristiano_Ajax.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ajax.jpg)[Cristiano Ronaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo "Cristiano Ronaldo") is Real Madrid's record goalscorer and the first player ever to score against every team in a single La Liga season.
Cristiano Ronaldo (2009–2018) is Real Madrid's all-time top goalscorer, with 450 goals in 438 matches.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-224)[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-225) Six other players have also scored over 200 goals for Real: [Alfredo Di Stéfano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano "Alfredo Di Stéfano") (1953–1964), [Santillana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santillana_\(footballer\) "Santillana \(footballer\)") (1971–1988), [Ferenc Puskás](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferenc_Pusk%C3%A1s "Ferenc Puskás") (1958–1966), [Hugo Sánchez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_S%C3%A1nchez "Hugo Sánchez") (1985–1992), [Karim Benzema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karim_Benzema "Karim Benzema") (2009–2023) and the previous goalscoring record-holder Raúl (1994–2010). Cristiano Ronaldo also holds the record for the most league goals scored in one season (48 in 2014–15), alongside being Real's top goalscorer of all time in [La Liga history with 311 goals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Liga#Most_goals "La Liga"). Di Stéfano's 49 goals in 58 matches was for decades the all-time highest tally in the European Cup, until it was surpassed by Raúl in 2005, and is now held by Cristiano Ronaldo with 105 goals for Madrid and 140 overall. The fastest goal in the history of the club (13 seconds) was scored by the Chilean [Iván Zamorano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Zamorano "Iván Zamorano") on 3 September 1994 during a league match against [Sevilla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sevilla_FC "Sevilla FC").[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-226)
Officially, the highest home attendance figure for a Real Madrid match is 129,690, which was for a European Cup match in 1956 against [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AC_Milan "AC Milan"). The current official capacity of the Santiago Bernabéu is 80,000.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-227) Real has also set records in Spanish football, most notably the most domestic titles (36 as of 2023–24) and the most seasons won in a row (five, during 1960–65 and 1985–90).[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_Club_de_Fútbol-1) With 121 matches (from 17 February 1957 to 7 March 1965), the club holds the record for longest unbeaten run at home in La Liga.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-228)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gareth_Bale_2015_%289%29.jpg/250px-Gareth_Bale_2015_%289%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gareth_Bale_2015_\(9\).jpg)[Gareth Bale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gareth_Bale "Gareth Bale") is the club's joint record signing, costing €100 million in 2013.
The club also holds the record for winning the [European Cup/UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League "UEFA Champions League") fifteen times[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-229) and for the [most semi-finals appearances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Cup_and_UEFA_Champions_League_records_and_statistics#By_semi-final_appearances "European Cup and UEFA Champions League records and statistics") (33). As of June 2024, Cristiano Ronaldo is the [all-time top scorer in the UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_top_scorers "List of UEFA Champions League top scorers"), with 140 (141 including qualifiers) goals in total, 105 while playing for Real Madrid. The team has the record number of [consecutive participations in the European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Cup_and_UEFA_Champions_League_records_and_statistics#Consecutive_appearances "European Cup and UEFA Champions League records and statistics") (before it became the Champions League) with 15, from 1955–56 to 1969–70.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-230) Among the club's on-field records is a 22-game winning streak in all competitions during the [2014–15 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Real_Madrid_CF_season "2014–15 Real Madrid CF season"), a Spanish record. In September 2017, the club equalled the record of the Brazilian club [Santos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santos_FC "Santos FC"), starring [Pelé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pel%C3%A9 "Pelé"), by scoring in their 73rd consecutive game, before [Bayern Munich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich "FC Bayern Munich") breaks the record in 2021.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-231)
In June 2009, the club broke its own record for the [highest transfer fee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transfer_\(association_football\)#Highest_fees "Transfer \(association football\)") ever paid in the history of football after purchasing Manchester United star Cristiano Ronaldo for €94 million ([£](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pound_sterling "Pound sterling")80 million).[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-232)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-233) The fee of €77.5 million (100 billion lire) for Zinedine Zidane's transfer from [Juventus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juventus_FC "Juventus FC") to Real Madrid in 2001 was the previous highest transfer fee ever paid. This record (in pounds sterling) had been broken previously in June 2009, for a few days, when Real Madrid agreed to buy [Kaká](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kak%C3%A1 "Kaká") from [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.C._Milan "A.C. Milan") for €67 million (£65 million). The transfer of [Tottenham Hotspur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C. "Tottenham Hotspur F.C.")'s [Gareth Bale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gareth_Bale "Gareth Bale") in 2013 was reportedly a new world record signing, with the transfer fee approximated at around €100 million.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-realmadrid2-111) In January 2016, documents pertaining to Bale's transfer were leaked which confirmed a world record transfer fee of €100,759,418.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-234) Real Madrid equalled their record signing in 2019, when the club signed [Eden Hazard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eden_Hazard "Eden Hazard") from [Chelsea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chelsea_F.C. "Chelsea F.C.") for a reported €115 million.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-235) The club's record sale occurred on 10 July 2018, when [Juventus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juventus_FC "Juventus FC") signed Cristiano Ronaldo for €117 million.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-236)
## Support
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium%2C_September_2014_07.JPG/250px-Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium%2C_September_2014_07.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium,_September_2014_07.JPG)The number of season tickets at the Bernabéu is capped at 65,000, with the remaining seats made available to the general public.
During most home matches, the majority of the seats in the stadium are occupied by season-ticket holders, of which the figure is capped at 65,000.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-237) To become a season ticket holder one must first be a _socio_ , or club member. In addition to members, the club has more than 1,800  _peñas_ (official, club-affiliated supporters' groups) in Spain and around the world. Real Madrid has the second highest average all-time attendance in Spanish football and regularly attracts over 74,000 fans to the [Bernabéu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium"). One of the best supported teams globally, Real Madrid was the first sports team (and first brand) to reach 100 million fans on Facebook in April 2017.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-238)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-239)
Real Madrid's hardcore supporters are the so-called _Ultras Sur_ supporters, or simply Ultras. They are known for their extreme [right-wing politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_politics "Right-wing politics"), akin to Barcelona's hardcore supporters group [Boixos Nois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boixos_Nois "Boixos Nois"). The Ultras Surs have developed an alliance with other right wing groups, most notably [Lazio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S.S._Lazio "S.S. Lazio") _[Irriducibili](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S.S._Lazio_fans "S.S. Lazio fans")_ fans, and have also developed an alliance with left-wing groups. On several occasions, they have racially abused opposing players, and have been investigated by UEFA for doing so.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-240)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-241) [Florentino Pérez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florentino_P%C3%A9rez "Florentino Pérez") took it upon himself to ban the Ultras from the Bernabéu and assign their seats to the general public. This decision was controversial with some of the Bernabéu faithful, however, as the lively atmosphere of games would suffer as a result.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-242)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-243) The Ultras have since held protests outside the Bernabéu and have demanded to be reinstated and allowed to enter the grounds.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-244)
Questioned over [Pope Francis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Francis "Pope Francis")' adherence to [2014 FIFA Club World Cup Final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final "2014 FIFA Club World Cup Final") opponents [San Lorenzo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Lorenzo_de_Almagro "San Lorenzo de Almagro"), Madrid captain [Sergio Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Ramos "Sergio Ramos") stated: "In the [semi-finals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_FIFA_Club_World_Cup#Semi-finals "2014 FIFA Club World Cup") we noticed the love from supporters in [Marrakesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marrakesh "Marrakesh") and it seemed like we were playing at home. That sums up the greatness of this team. Madrid is [God](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/God_in_Christianity "God in Christianity")'s team and the team of the world".[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-245) Among the club's famous supporters is golfer [Sergio García](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Garc%C3%ADa "Sergio García"), who was invited to take the honorary kickoff for El Clásico at the Bernabeu wearing his green jacket from winning the [2017 Masters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Masters_Tournament "2017 Masters Tournament").[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-246)
## Rivalries
### El Clásico
Main article: [El Clásico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Cl%C3%A1sico "El Clásico")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Control_de_Sergio_%285628131065%29.jpg/250px-Control_de_Sergio_%285628131065%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Control_de_Sergio_\(5628131065\).jpg)Scene from a 2011 _[El Clásico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Cl%C3%A1sico "El Clásico")_ at the Santiago Bernabéu Stadium
There is often a fierce rivalry between the two strongest teams in a national league, and this is particularly the case in La Liga, where the game between Real Madrid and [Barcelona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona "FC Barcelona") is known as "The Classic" (_El Clásico_). From the start of national competitions the clubs were seen as representatives of two rival regions in Spain: [Castile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castile_\(historical_region\) "Castile \(historical region\)") and [Catalonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalonia "Catalonia"), as well as of the two cities. The rivalry reflects what many regard as the political and cultural tensions felt between the [Castilians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castilians "Castilians") and [Catalans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_people "Catalan people"), seen by one author as a re-enactment of the [Spanish Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War "Spanish Civil War").[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-247) Over the years, the record for Real Madrid and Barcelona is 105 victories for Madrid, 101 victories for Barcelona, and 52 draws as of December 2024.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-248)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Real_Madrid_-_Bar%C3%A7a_%283495454182%29.jpg/250px-Real_Madrid_-_Bar%C3%A7a_%283495454182%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Real_Madrid_-_Bar%C3%A7a_\(3495454182\).jpg)Real Madrid fans displaying the white of their club before _El Clásico_. Real Madrid fans also often wave [Spanish flags](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Spain "Flag of Spain") at _El Clásico_ games.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-249)
As early as the 1930s, Barcelona "had developed a reputation as a symbol of Catalan identity, opposed to the centralising tendencies of Madrid".[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-josepsunyol-250)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-251) During the dictatorships of [Miguel Primo de Rivera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miguel_Primo_de_Rivera "Miguel Primo de Rivera") and especially [Francisco Franco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Franco "Francisco Franco"), all regional languages and identities in Spain were frowned upon and restrained. As such, most citizens of Barcelona were in strong opposition to [Franco's regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francoist_Spain "Francoist Spain"). In that period, Barcelona gained their motto _Més que un club_ (_English: More than a club_) because of its alleged connection to [Catalan nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_nationalism "Catalan nationalism") as well as to [progressive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressivism "Progressivism") beliefs.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-252)
There is an ongoing controversy as to what extent Franco's rule (1939–75) influenced the activities and on-pitch results of both Barcelona and Real Madrid. Fans of both clubs tend to exaggerate the myths favouring their narratives. Most historians agree that Franco did not have a preferred football team, but his Spanish nationalist beliefs led him to associate himself with the establishment teams, such as [Atlético Aviación](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid "Atlético Madrid") and Madrid FC (that recovered its "royal" name after the fall of the Republic and again became Real Madrid). On the other hand, he also wanted the renamed Barcelona succeed as "Spanish team", rather than a Catalan one. During the early years of Franco's rule, Real Madrid were not particularly successful, winning two [Copa del Generalísimo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_del_Rey "Copa del Rey") titles and a [Copa Eva Duarte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_Eva_Duarte "Copa Eva Duarte"); Barcelona claimed three [league titles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Spanish_football_champions "List of Spanish football champions"), one Copa del Generalísimo and one Copa Eva Duarte. During that period, Atlético Aviación were believed to be the preferred team over Real Madrid. The most contested stories of the period include Real Madrid's [11–1 home win against Barcelona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#Early_years_\(1902–1943\)) in the [Copa del Generalísimo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1943_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo "1943 Copa del Generalísimo"), where the Catalan team alleged intimidation, and the controversial transfer of [Alfredo Di Stéfano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano "Alfredo Di Stéfano") to Real Madrid, despite his agreement with Barcelona. The latter transfer was part of Real Madrid chairman [Santiago Bernabéu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_\(footballer\) "Santiago Bernabéu \(footballer\)")'s "revolution" that ushered in the era of unprecedented dominance. Bernabéu, himself a veteran of the Civil War who fought for [Franco's forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_faction_\(Spanish_Civil_War\) "Nationalist faction \(Spanish Civil War\)"), saw Real Madrid on top, not only of Spanish, but also European football, helping create the [European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League "UEFA Champions League"), the first true competition for Europe's best club sides. His vision was fulfilled when Real Madrid not only started winning consecutive league titles, but also swept the first five editions of the European Cup in the 1950s.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-253) These events had a profound impact on Spanish football and influenced Franco's attitude. According to historians, during this time he realized the importance of Real Madrid for his regime's international image, and the club became his preferred team until his death. [Fernando Maria Castiella](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fernando_Maria_Castiella "Fernando Maria Castiella"), who served as [minister of foreign affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Spain\) "Minister of Foreign Affairs \(Spain\)") under Franco from 1957 until 1969, noted that "[Real Madrid] is the best embassy we have ever had". Franco died in 1975, and the [Spanish transition to democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy "Spanish transition to democracy") soon followed. Under his rule, [Real Madrid had won](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Real_Madrid_CF_records_and_statistics#Honours "List of Real Madrid CF records and statistics") 14 league titles, six Copa del Generalísimo titles, one Copa Eva Duarte, six European Cups, two [Latin Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_Cup "Latin Cup") and one [Intercontinental Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_\(1960%E2%80%932004\) "Intercontinental Cup \(1960–2004\)"). In the same period, [Barcelona had won](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FC_Barcelona_records_and_statistics#Honours "List of FC Barcelona records and statistics") eight league titles, nine Copa del Generalísimo titles, three Copa Eva Duarte titles, three [Inter-Cities Fairs Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup "Inter-Cities Fairs Cup") and two Latin Cups.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-254)[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-goal.com-186)
The rivalry was intensified during the 1950s when the clubs disputed the signing of Alfredo Di Stéfano. Di Stéfano had impressed both Barcelona and Real Madrid while playing for [Los Millonarios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Los_Millonarios "Club Deportivo Los Millonarios") in [Bogotá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1 "Bogotá"), [Colombia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colombia "Colombia"), during a players' strike in his native [Argentina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina "Argentina"). Soon after Millonarios' return to Colombia, Barcelona directors visited Buenos Aires and agreed with River Plate, the last FIFA-affiliated team to have held Di Stéfano's rights, for his transfer in 1954 for the equivalent of 150 million Italian lira (according to other sources 200,000 dollars). This started a battle between the two Spanish rivals for his rights. FIFA appointed Armando Muñoz Calero, former president of the Spanish Football Federation as mediator. Calero decided to let Di Stéfano play the 1953–54 and 1955–56 seasons in Madrid, and the 1954–55 and 1956–57 seasons in Barcelona. The agreement was approved by the Football Association and their respective clubs. Although the Catalans agreed, the decision created various discontent among the Blaugrana members and the president was forced to resign in September 1953. Barcelona sold Madrid their half-share, and Di Stéfano moved to _Los Blancos_ , signing a four-year contract. Real paid 5.5 million Spanish pesetas for the transfer, plus a 1.3 million bonus for the purchase, an annual fee to be paid to the Millonarios, and a 16,000 salary for Di Stéfano with a bonus double that of his teammates, for a total of 40% of the annual revenue of the Madrid club.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-di_Stefano-255)
Di Stéfano became integral in the subsequent success achieved by Real Madrid, scoring twice in his first game against Barcelona. With him, Madrid won the first five editions of the European Cup.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-256) The 1960s saw the rivalry reach the European stage when Real Madrid and Barcelona met twice in the European Cup, with Madrid triumphing en route to their fifth consecutive title in [1959–60](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959%E2%80%9360_European_Cup "1959–60 European Cup") and Barcelona prevailing en route to losing the final in [1960–61](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960%E2%80%9361_European_Cup "1960–61 European Cup"). Ahead of the 1973–74 season, [Johan Cruyff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johan_Cruyff "Johan Cruyff") arrived to Barcelona for a world record £920,000 from [Ajax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AFC_Ajax "AFC Ajax").[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-257) Already an established player with Ajax, Cruyff quickly won over the Barcelona fans when he told the European press that he chose Barcelona over Real Madrid because he could not play for a club associated with Francisco Franco. He further endeared himself when he named his son ["Jordi"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordi_Cruyff "Jordi Cruyff"), after the local Catalan [Saint George](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_George "Saint George").[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-258) In 2002, the [European encounter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_stage#Semi-finals "2001–02 UEFA Champions League knockout stage") between the clubs was dubbed the "Match of The Century" by Spanish media, and Madrid's win was watched by more than 500 million people around the world.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-259) A fixture known for its intensity and indiscipline, it has also featured [memorable goal celebrations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal_celebration "Goal celebration") from both teams, often involving mocking the opposition.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Marca-260) In October 1999, Real Madrid forward [Raúl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_\(footballer\) "Raúl \(footballer\)") silenced 100,000 Barcelona fans at the Camp Nou when he scored before he celebrated by putting a finger to his lips as if telling the crowd to be quiet.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Marca-260)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-261) In 2009, Barcelona captain [Carles Puyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carles_Puyol "Carles Puyol") kissed his Catalan armband in front of Madrid fans at the Bernabéu.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Marca-260) Cristiano Ronaldo twice gestured to the hostile crowd to "calm down" after scoring against Barcelona at the Camp Nou in 2012 and 2016.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Marca-260) In April 2017, Messi celebrated his 93rd-minute winner for Barcelona against Real Madrid at the Bernabéu by taking off his Barcelona shirt and holding it up to incensed Real Madrid fans – with his name and number facing them.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Marca-260) Later that year, in August, Ronaldo was subbed on in the first leg of the [Supercopa de España](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a "2017 Supercopa de España"), proceeded to score in the 80th minute and took his shirt off before holding it up to Barça's fans with his name and number facing them.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-262)
### El Derbi madrileño
Main article: [Madrid derby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrid_derby "Madrid derby")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bernabeu_en_un_Madrid-Atleti.JPG/250px-Bernabeu_en_un_Madrid-Atleti.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bernabeu_en_un_Madrid-Atleti.JPG)Real Madrid supporters during the 2006 _El Derbi madrileño_ match held at the Santiago Bernabéu
The club's nearest neighbour is [Atlético Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid "Atlético Madrid"), a rivalry being shared between fans of both football teams. Although Atlético was founded by three [Basque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basque_people "Basque people") students in 1903, it was joined in 1904 by dissident members of "Madrid FC". The two teams met for the first time on 2 December 1906 in the [regional championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campeonato_Regional_Centro#1906–07 "Campeonato Regional Centro"), with Real Madrid winning 2–1. Their first league meeting came on 21 February 1929 in matchday three of the first [league championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_La_Liga "1929 La Liga") at the former [Chamartín](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadio_Chamart%C3%ADn "Estadio Chamartín"). It was the first official derby of the new tournament, and Real won 2–1.[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Real_Madrid_turns_106_\(III\)-47) After the Civil War, during the early [Francoist period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francoist_Spain "Francoist Spain"), Atlético became associated with the [military air force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Air_Force "Spanish Air Force") (and thus renamed Atlético Aviación), although the alleged preference of the regime for the club is subject to discussion. In any case, during this period Atlético became the most successful club in Spain, reducing the historical gap between the two clubs, until the regime preference shifted towards Real Madrid in the 1950s, as Franco sought to make political capital out of Real Madrid's multiple [European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League "UEFA Champions League") titles at a time when Spain was internationally isolated; one minister said, "Real Madrid are the best ambassadors we've ever had."[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-goal.com-186) Thus, Atlético fans regularly chanted that Real were _"El equipo del gobierno, la vergüenza del país"_ – "The team of the government, the shame of the country" – and allegedly adopted a more [left-wing slant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_politics "Left-wing politics") (tempered by the rise of [ultras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultras "Ultras") culture and [Rayo Vallecano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rayo_Vallecano "Rayo Vallecano")'s presence as the "true" leftist club in Madrid).[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-263)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-struggle-264)
The rivalry first gained international attention in 1959 during the [European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958%E2%80%9359_European_Cup "1958–59 European Cup") when the two clubs met in the semi-finals. Real won the first leg 2–1 at the [Santiago Bernabéu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium"), while Atlético won 1–0 at the [Metropolitano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadio_Metropolitano_de_Madrid "Estadio Metropolitano de Madrid"). The tie went to a replay, which Real won 2–1. Atlético, however, gained some revenge when, led by former Real Madrid coach [José Villalonga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Villalonga_Llorente "José Villalonga Llorente"), it defeated its city rivals in two successive [Copa del Generalísimo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_del_Rey "Copa del Rey") finals in [1960](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo_Final "1960 Copa del Generalísimo Final") and [1961](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1961_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo_Final "1961 Copa del Generalísimo Final").[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-265) In the 1970s, Atlético again took the lead as the most successful Spanish club of the decade, which prompted the Real Madrid fanbase to look down on Atlético calling them and their supporters "Indios" ([Indians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas "Indigenous peoples of the Americas"), a reference to the [Latin American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America") players signed by the Red-and-whites).[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-266) By then, Real Madrid did not want to sign non-[Caucasian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasian_race "Caucasian race") players (president [Santiago Bernabéu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_\(footballer\) "Santiago Bernabéu \(footballer\)") even stated, when he decided not to sign Portuguese star [Eusebio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eusebio "Eusebio") at the end of the 1960s, _"Mientras yo viva, aquí no jugará ningún negro ni un blanco con bigote"_ ("As long as I live, no black or white with a mustache will play here").[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-267) Atlético's supporters accepted the new "Indian" nickname joyfully and have been using it until today. The Santiago Bernabéu, Real Madrid's stadium, is alongside banks and businesses on the [upper class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bourgeoisie "Bourgeoisie") [Paseo de la Castellana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Castellana "Paseo de la Castellana") street, while the [Vicente Calderón](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vicente_Calder%C3%B3n_Stadium "Vicente Calderón Stadium") (the stadium that Atlético Madrid used until the [2016–17 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid_season "2016–17 Atlético Madrid season")) could be found near a brewery, alongside the [Manzanares River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manzanares_\(river\) "Manzanares \(river\)") and a motorway. Real draw greater support all across the region because of their historically greater resources and success, while Atlético have a relatively [working class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Working_class "Working class") fan base mainly from the south of the city, with some fans also scattered throughout the city.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-268)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-269) In fact, the Atlético crest includes the [Coat of arms of Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Madrid "Coat of arms of Madrid"), whereas Real crest has no such a reference to the city (instead, it includes a reference to the broader [Castile region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castile_\(historical_region\) "Castile \(historical region\)")).
Between 1961 and 1989, when Real dominated La Liga, only Atlético offered it any serious challenge, winning league titles in 1966, 1970, 1973 and 1977. In 1965, Atlético became the first team to beat Real at the Bernabéu in eight years. Real Madrid's record against Atlético in more recent times has been favourable.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-270) A high point came in the [2002–03 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_La_Liga "2002–03 La Liga"), when Real clinched the La Liga title after a 4–0 victory at the Vicente Calderón. Atlético's first win over its city rivals since 1999 came in the [Copa del Rey final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_Copa_del_Rey_Final "2013 Copa del Rey Final") in May 2013. In [2013–14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League "2013–14 UEFA Champions League"), Real and Atlético were finalists of the UEFA Champions League, the first final which hosted two clubs from the same city. Real Madrid triumphed with a [4–1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2014 UEFA Champions League Final") comeback victory in extra time.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-271) On [7 February 2015](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_La_Liga "2014–15 La Liga"), Real suffered their first defeat in 14 years at the Vicente Calderón, a 4–0 loss.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-272) On [28 May 2016](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League "2015–16 UEFA Champions League"), Real and Atlético again met for the [Champions League title](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2016 UEFA Champions League Final"), which resulted in a win for Real after a penalty shootout at [San Siro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Siro "San Siro").[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-273)
### El Viejo Clásico
Main article: [El Viejo Clásico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Viejo_Cl%C3%A1sico "El Viejo Clásico")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Guti_%284591568690%29.jpg/250px-Guti_%284591568690%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Guti_\(4591568690\).jpg)Real Madrid's [Guti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guti_\(Spanish_footballer\) "Guti \(Spanish footballer\)") (left) and Athletic Bilbao's [Javi Martínez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Javi_Mart%C3%ADnez "Javi Martínez") (centre) and [Amorebieta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fernando_Amorebieta "Fernando Amorebieta") (right) during a match at the Bernabéu, 2010
A further minor rivalry exists between Real Madrid and [Athletic Bilbao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao "Athletic Bilbao"). This is known as [El Viejo Clásico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Viejo_Cl%C3%A1sico "El Viejo Clásico") (_the old classic_),[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-RTVE-274) so named as the two clubs were dominant in the first half of the 20th century, meeting in nine Copa del Rey finals including the first in [1903](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1903_Copa_del_Rey "1903 Copa del Rey").[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-275)[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-276) Until 10 December 2011, this fixture was the most played in the history of [Spanish football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football_in_Spain "Football in Spain"), when it was surpassed by _El Clásico_.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-277)
Athletic Bilbao, who operate a [policy of only using local players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao_signing_policy "Athletic Bilbao signing policy"),[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-278) have long since ceased to be a competitive rival to clubs such as Real Madrid who scour the globe for the best talent; the _Lions_ won only two of the 26 matches between the teams from [2005–06](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_La_Liga "2005–06 La Liga") to [2016–17](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_La_Liga "2016–17 La Liga").[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-RTVE-274)[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-ACpastliga-279)[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-BDFRMCF-280) However, the matches remain keenly fought due to their historical and cultural significance, with some parallels to the political aspect of the Barcelona/Catalonia rivalry as Athletic are the largest club in the [Basque region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basque_Country_\(greater_region\) "Basque Country \(greater region\)").[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-morboreview-281)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-struggle-264)[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-squid-282)
### European rivalries
See also: [Real Madrid CF in international football § European Cup / UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF_in_international_football#European_Cup_/_UEFA_Champions_League "Real Madrid CF in international football")
#### Bayern Munich
Main article: [Bayern Munich–Real Madrid rivalry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayern_Munich%E2%80%93Real_Madrid_rivalry "Bayern Munich–Real Madrid rivalry")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Real_Madrid_vs_Bayern_Munich.jpg/250px-Real_Madrid_vs_Bayern_Munich.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Real_Madrid_vs_Bayern_Munich.jpg)Real Madrid players celebrating a goal against Bayern Munich in [2007](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_stage#Round_of_16 "2006–07 UEFA Champions League knockout stage")
Real Madrid and [Bayern Munich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich "FC Bayern Munich") are two of the most successful clubs in the UEFA Champions League/European Cup competition, with Real winning 15 times and Bayern winning six times.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-283)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-284) Although they have never met in a final, Real Madrid versus Bayern is the match that has historically been played most often in the Champions League/European Cup with 26 matches (twelve wins for Madrid, eleven wins for Bayern, with three draws),[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-RMCF-FCB_H2H-285) with several controversial incidents occurring due to the great importance of most of their meetings.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-286)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-hunter17-287)[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-288) Real Madrid supporters often refer to Bayern as the "Bestia negra" ("Black Beast").
During the 2010s, the two teams met in the [2011–12 Champions League semi-finals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase#Semi-finals "2011–12 UEFA Champions League knockout phase"), which ended 3–3 on aggregate (Bayern won 3–1 on penalties after extra time, but lost [the final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2012 UEFA Champions League Final") at their own stadium by the same method), then at the same stage in the [2013–14 edition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase#Semi-finals "2013–14 UEFA Champions League knockout phase") with Real Madrid winning 5–0 on aggregate,[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-289) and again in [2017–18](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase#Semi-finals "2017–18 UEFA Champions League knockout phase") with the Spanish club progressing 4–3;[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-290) both times they went on to win the competition.
#### Juventus
Another match that is often played in the European Cup/Champions League is Real Madrid vs [Juventus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juventus_FC "Juventus FC"), the most decorated Italian club. They have played each other in 21 matches and have an almost perfectly balanced record (nine wins for Juventus, ten wins for Real Madrid and two draws), as well as nearly the same goal difference (Madrid ahead 26 to 25).[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-uefajuve-291)[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-secondmost-293)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/UEFA_Champions_League_Final_Cardiff_2017.jpg/250px-UEFA_Champions_League_Final_Cardiff_2017.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:UEFA_Champions_League_Final_Cardiff_2017.jpg)Pre-match display at the [2017 Champions League final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2017 UEFA Champions League Final") between Real Madrid and Juventus
Their first meeting was in the quarter-finals of the [1961–62 European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_European_Cup "1961–62 European Cup"), which Real Madrid won 3–1 in a replay held in [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris "Paris").[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292) At the quarter-final stage in [1995–96](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_UEFA_Champions_League "1995–96 UEFA Champions League"), Juventus prevailed 2–1 over the two legs and went on to lift the trophy.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292) In the [1998 UEFA Champions League Final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "1998 UEFA Champions League Final") between the teams in [Amsterdam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amsterdam "Amsterdam"), Real Madrid won 1–0.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-294) They met again in the [2002–03 UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_UEFA_Champions_League "2002–03 UEFA Champions League") semi-finals, when both clubs were in their respective 'golden eras'; Juventus won 4–3 on aggregate.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292) By that time, star midfielder [Zinedine Zidane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane "Zinedine Zidane"), who played for the _Bianconeri_ in the 1998 final, had moved from [Turin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turin "Turin") to Madrid in a world record €77 million deal.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-295)
The teams met again in the [2013–14 UEFA Champions League group stage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage "2013–14 UEFA Champions League group stage"), with Madrid winning 2–1 at home and drawing 2–2 away en route to their tenth title. In the [2014–15 UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League "2014–15 UEFA Champions League") semi-finals, former Real Madrid player [Álvaro Morata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Morata "Álvaro Morata") scored one goal in each leg to take Juventus to the final, winning 3–2 on aggregate, while Cristiano Ronaldo scored both goals for Madrid.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292) They faced off again in the [2017 UEFA Champions League Final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "2017 UEFA Champions League Final") in [Cardiff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardiff "Cardiff"), with Ronaldo scoring twice as Real Madrid won 4–1.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-bdfrmjuv-292)[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-296)[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-297)
The latest Champions League meeting was in the [2017–18 quarter-finals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase#Quarter-finals "2017–18 UEFA Champions League knockout phase"), which Real Madrid won 4–3 on aggregate; the tie ended in dramatic and controversial fashion, with a debatable penalty awarded to Real Madrid in the last minute of the second leg after Juventus built a 3–0 lead at the Bernabeu to pull level in the tie following a defeat at the [Allianz Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Juventus_Stadium "Juventus Stadium") by the same scoreline.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-298)[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-299) Cristiano Ronaldo scored three goals over the two matches including the decisive penalty and a spectacular overhead kick,[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-300) and having won the Champions League with Madrid for a fourth time,[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-3rdCL-301) he transferred to Juventus a few months later for a €117 million fee.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-302)
## Finances and ownership
It was under [Florentino Pérez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florentino_P%C3%A9rez "Florentino Pérez")'s first presidency (2000–2006) that Real Madrid started its ambition of becoming the world's richest professional football club.[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-303) The club ceded part of its training grounds to the city of Madrid in 2001, and sold the rest to four corporations: Repsol YPF, Mutua Automovilística de Madrid, Sacyr Vallehermoso and OHL. The sale eradicated the club's debts, paving the way for it to buy the world's most expensive players, such as [Zinedine Zidane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane "Zinedine Zidane"), [Luís Figo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo "Luís Figo"), [Ronaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronaldo_\(Brazilian_footballer\) "Ronaldo \(Brazilian footballer\)") and [David Beckham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Beckham "David Beckham"). The city had previously rezoned the training grounds for development, a move which in turn increased their value, and then bought the site.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-2001-2010-79) The [European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") started an investigation into whether the city overpaid for the property, to be considered a form of state subsidy.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-304)
The sale of the training ground for office buildings cleared Real Madrid's debts of €270 million and enabled the club to embark upon an unprecedented spending spree which brought big-name players to the club. In addition, profit from the sale was spent on a state-of-the-art training complex on the city's outskirts.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-305) Although Pérez's policy resulted in increased financial success from the exploitation of the club's high marketing potential around the world, especially in Asia, it came under increasing criticism for being too focused on marketing the Real Madrid brand and not enough on the performances of the team.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Lowe-82)
By September 2007, Real Madrid was considered the most valuable football brand in Europe by [BBDO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBDO "BBDO"). In 2008, it was ranked the second-most valuable club in world football, at €951 million (£640 million / $1.285 billion),[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-306) only beaten by Manchester United, which was valued at €1.333 billion (£900 million).[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-The_Most_Valuable_Soccer_Teams_—_Manchester_United-307) In 2010, Real Madrid had the highest turnover in football worldwide.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-308) In September 2009, Real Madrid's management announced plans to open the club's own dedicated theme park by 2013.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-309)
A study at [Harvard University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harvard_University "Harvard University") concluded that Real Madrid "is one of the 20 most important brand names and the only one in which its executives, the players, are well-known. We have some spectacular figures in regard to worldwide support of the club. There are an estimated 287 million people worldwide who follow Real Madrid."[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-310) In 2010, _[Forbes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ evaluated Real Madrid's worth to be around €992 million (US$1.323 billion), ranking them second only to Manchester United, based on figures from the 2008–09 season.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-311)[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-312) According to [Deloitte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deloitte "Deloitte"), Real Madrid had a recorded revenue of €401 million in the same period, ranking first.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-313)
Along with Barcelona, Athletic Bilbao and [Osasuna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CA_Osasuna "CA Osasuna"), Real Madrid is organised as a registered association. This means that the club is owned by its supporters, who elect the president. The president cannot invest his own money,[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-314) and the club can only spend what it earns, which is mainly derived through sponsorships, commercial partnerships, merchandise sales, television rights, prize money and ticket sales. Unlike a [limited company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limited_company "Limited company"), it is not possible to purchase shares in the club, but only a membership.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-315) The members of Real Madrid, called "socios", form an assembly of delegates which is the highest governing body of the club.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-316) As of 2010, the club had 60,000 _socios_.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-317) At the end of the 2009–10 season, the club's board of directors stated that Real Madrid had a net debt of €244.6 million, €82.1 million lower than the previous fiscal year. Real Madrid announced that it had a net debt of €170 million after the 2010–11 season. From 2007 to 2011, the club made a net profit of €190 million.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-blogspot1-318)[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-319)
During the 2009–10 season, Real Madrid made €150 million through ticket sales, the most of any club in top-flight football.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-blogspot1-318) Real Madrid has the highest number of shirt sales per season, around 1.5 million.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-blogspot1-318) For the 2010–11 season, Madrid's wage bill totalled €169 million, which was second-highest in Europe behind Barcelona;[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-320) furthermore, its wage bill to turnover ratio was the best in Europe at 43 percent, ahead of Manchester United and Arsenal at 46 percent and 50 percent, respectively. In 2013, _Forbes_ listed the club as the world's most valuable sports team, worth $3.3 billion.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-321) Real Madrid was valued at €3.47 billion ($4.1 billion) in 2018, and in the 2016–17 season it was the [second highest-earning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deloitte_Football_Money_League "Deloitte Football Money League") football club in the world, with an annual revenue of €674.6 million.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Deloitte-322) In November 2018, the average first-team pay at Madrid was £8.1m ($10.6m) per year, making it the second-highest paid sports team in the world after Barcelona.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-323)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-324) In 2022, _Forbes_ listed Real Madrid as the most valuable football club in the world, at $5.1 billion.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-:0-325)
## Popular culture
Real Madrid was the featured club in the second installment of the _[Goal!](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal!_\(film\) "Goal! \(film\)")_ football movie trilogy, _[Goal! 2: Living the Dream...](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal!_2:_Living_the_Dream... "Goal! 2: Living the Dream...")_ (2007). The film follows former [Newcastle United](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C. "Newcastle United F.C.") star Santiago Muñez as he is first scouted and then signed by Real Madrid for the 2005–06 season. The film's creators wanted to put emphasis on the changes in Muñez's life after his move to Madrid. Production was done with the full support of UEFA, allowing the film crew to use many real life players in cameo roles. Real Madrid squad members featured in the film included [Iker Casillas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iker_Casillas "Iker Casillas"), [Zinedine Zidane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane "Zinedine Zidane"), [David Beckham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Beckham "David Beckham"), [Ronaldo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronaldo_\(Brazilian_footballer\) "Ronaldo \(Brazilian footballer\)"), [Roberto Carlos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roberto_Carlos "Roberto Carlos"), [Raúl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_\(footballer\) "Raúl \(footballer\)"), [Sergio Ramos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Ramos "Sergio Ramos"), [Robinho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robinho "Robinho"), [Michael Owen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Owen "Michael Owen"), [Míchel Salgado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%ADchel_Salgado "Míchel Salgado"), [Júlio Baptista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_Baptista "Júlio Baptista"), [Steve McManaman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_McManaman "Steve McManaman") and [Iván Helguera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Helguera "Iván Helguera"). Non-Real Madrid players to make cameo appearances included [Ronaldinho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronaldinho "Ronaldinho"), [Thierry Henry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thierry_Henry "Thierry Henry"), [Lionel Messi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Messi "Lionel Messi"), [Samuel Eto'o](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Eto%27o "Samuel Eto'o"), [Andrés Iniesta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Iniesta "Andrés Iniesta"), [Pablo Aimar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pablo_Aimar "Pablo Aimar"), [Freddie Ljungberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freddie_Ljungberg "Freddie Ljungberg"), [Cesc Fàbregas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas "Cesc Fàbregas") and [Santiago Cañizares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Ca%C3%B1izares "Santiago Cañizares"). In the film, both [Florentino Pérez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florentino_P%C3%A9rez "Florentino Pérez") and [Alfredo Di Stéfano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano "Alfredo Di Stéfano") presented the fictional player Muñez to the club after his signing.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-326)
_Real, The Movie_ is a 2005 part feature, part documentary film that showcases the worldwide passion for Real Madrid. Produced by the club and directed by Borja Manso, it follows five sub-stories of fans from around the world and their love for the club. Along with the fictional portion of the film, it also contains real footage of the squad, during training at [Ciudad Real Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciudad_Real_Madrid "Ciudad Real Madrid"), matches, and interviews. Although the film mentions all of the squad, it mainly focuses on [_galácticos_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gal%C3%A1ctico "Galáctico") such as David Beckham, Zinedine Zidane, Raúl, Luís Figo, Ronaldo, Iker Casillas and Roberto Carlos, among others. The film was originally produced in Spanish, but has been dubbed for their worldwide fanbase.
The book _White Storm: 100 years of Real Madrid_ by [Phil Ball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phil_Ball_\(writer\) "Phil Ball \(writer\)") was the first English-language history of Real Madrid. Published in 2002, it talks about the most successful moments of the club during its first centenary, having been translated into various languages. In late 2011, Real Madrid released a digital music album, entitled _Legends_ , and a remix of the club's anthem, "Himno del Real Madrid," was released as the first single from the album.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-327)
### Real Madrid TV
[Real Madrid TV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_TV "Real Madrid TV") is an encrypted [digital television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_television "Digital television") channel, operated by Real Madrid and specialising in the club. The channel is available in Spanish and English. It is located at [Ciudad Real Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciudad_Real_Madrid "Ciudad Real Madrid") in Valdebebas (Madrid), Real Madrid's training centre.
### _Hala Madrid_
"Hala Madrid" redirects here. For the club's anthem, see [Hala Madrid y nada más](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hala_Madrid_y_nada_m%C3%A1s "Hala Madrid y nada más").
_Hala Madrid_ is a magazine published quarterly for the Real Madrid club members and the _Madridistas Fan Club_ card holders.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Hala-328) The phrase Hala Madrid, meaning "Forward Madrid" or "Go Madrid", is also the title of the club's official anthem, which is often sung by the Madridistas (the club's fans).[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-uefa.com-6) The magazine includes reports on the club's matches in the previous month, as well as information about the reserve and youth teams. Features often include interviews with players, both past and present, and the club's historic matches.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Hala-328)
### Video games
Real Madrid has appeared in many football-based video games, namely in the [FIFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_\(video_game_series\) "FIFA \(video game series\)"), [EA Sports FC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EA_Sports_FC "EA Sports FC"), and [Pro Evolution Soccer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pro_Evolution_Soccer "Pro Evolution Soccer") series. A Real Madrid player has appeared on the cover of both titles a combined seven times.
In 2007, Spanish game publisher [Virgin Play](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin_Play "Virgin Play") signed a deal with the club to make officially licensed Real Madrid video games. The only one released under the deal (due to Virgin Play's liquidation in September 2009) would end up being _Real Madrid: The Game_ , which was developed by [Atomic Planet Entertainment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_Planet_Entertainment "Atomic Planet Entertainment") and was published under Virgin Play's publishing division [V.2 Play](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V.2_Play "V.2 Play") in May 2009 for the [PlayStation 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PlayStation_2 "PlayStation 2"), [PlayStation Portable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PlayStation_Portable "PlayStation Portable"), [Windows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows "Windows"), [Wii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wii "Wii") and [Nintendo DS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nintendo_DS "Nintendo DS") exclusively in European territories Virgin Play released their products in. The game featured a career mode with a mixture of role-playing and simulation as well as arcade-styled Football gameplay.

## Players
Main article: [List of Real Madrid CF players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Real_Madrid_CF_players "List of Real Madrid CF players")
For a list of all former and current Real Madrid CF players with a Wikipedia article, see [Category:Real Madrid CF players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Real_Madrid_CF_players "Category:Real Madrid CF players").
Spanish teams are limited to three players without EU citizenship. The squad list includes only the principal nationality of each player; several non-European players on the squad have dual citizenship with an EU country. Also, players from the [ACP countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ACP_countries "ACP countries") in Africa, the Caribbean, and the Pacific that are signatories to the [Cotonou Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement "Cotonou Agreement") are not counted against non-EU quotas due to the [Kolpak ruling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kolpak_ruling "Kolpak ruling").

## Notes
  1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_ref-Club_World_Cup_17-0 "Jump up")** Real Madrid have won five [FIFA Club World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup "FIFA Club World Cup"), three [Intercontinental Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_\(1960%E2%80%932004\) "Intercontinental Cup \(1960–2004\)") and one [FIFA Intercontinental Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Intercontinental_Cup "FIFA Intercontinental Cup") title for a total of nine.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-14) Additionally, Real Madrid won a one-off [Ibero-American Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_Iberoamericana "Copa Iberoamericana") (contested by [Copa de Oro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993_Copa_de_Oro "1993 Copa de Oro") and [Copa del Rey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Copa_del_Rey "1992–93 Copa del Rey") winners) in 1994.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Ibero-American_1-15)[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_note-Ibero-American_2-16)
  2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_ref-CdR_49-0 "Jump up")** The Copa del Rey, as it was known for the most part of its history, was renamed to _Copa del Presidente de la República_ by the Second Spanish Republic in 1932 and then to _Copa del Generalísimo_ by the Francoist government in 1939.
  3. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_ref-Origin_187-0 "Jump up")** Real Madrid home kit in 1905 was all-white, so the supporters began referring to the players as _Los Blancos._
  4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF#cite_ref-Kit_199-0 "Jump up")** Realmadrid.com appeared as shirt sponsor to promote the club's new website.
